## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material, which is a core problem in solid mechanics and materials science. Temperature typically modifies elastic modulus, yield behavior, and can introduce nonlinear effects such as thermal softening or phase transitions.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear elastic (Hooke's law): sigma = c0 * epsilon (basic linear stress-strain at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 - c2 * T) (linear elasticity with thermal softening of modulus)
- Thermal stress offset: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * T) (stress with thermal expansion strain subtraction)
- Full thermoelastic: sigma = c0 * (c1 - c2 * T) * (epsilon - c3 * T) (temperature-dependent modulus with thermal strain)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear stress-strain, Ramberg-Osgood type)
- Temperature-dependent power law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (power-law with Arrhenius-type thermal factor)
- Johnson-Cook type: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T) (strain hardening with thermal softening)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(-c1 * T) (modulus decreasing exponentially with temperature)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (nonlinear elastic with higher-order terms)
- Voce-type saturation hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * epsilon)) * (c2 - c3 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal softening)
- Arrhenius modulus: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 / T) (thermally activated modulus behavior)
- Hyperbolic sine flow: sigma = c0 * T * asinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 / T)) (Garofalo/Sellars-Tegart creep model)
- Bilinear with temperature: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 + c2 / (c3 + T)) (modulus with rational temperature dependence)
- Ludwik model with temperature: sigma = c0 * (c1 + epsilon)**c2 * exp(-c3 * T) (generalized hardening with thermal factor)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening of elastic modulus → Multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or exp(-c*T) applied to stress-strain relation
- Thermal expansion strain → Additive correction (epsilon - c*T) representing free thermal strain subtraction
- Strain hardening saturation → (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) form indicating asymptotic stress plateau
- Thermally activated deformation → Arrhenius factor exp(c/T) or exp(-c/T) reflecting diffusion-controlled mechanisms
- Phase transition or abrupt property change → Sigmoidal dependence on T such as tanh(c0*(T - c1)) for transition temperature
- Rate-independent plasticity → Piecewise or max-type functions of strain representing elastic-plastic transition
- Polynomial strain energy → Stress as derivative of polynomial in epsilon, giving odd-power series in epsilon
- Competing hardening and softening → Product of increasing function of epsilon and decreasing function of T

`T*c0*(c1+epsilon)³ + T*c2 + c3*epsilon/(c4*epsilon+c5) + c6/(c4*epsilon+c5) + c7*exp(c8*epsilon) + c9`

With c1=0, c4=0, c8=0: T*c0*epsilon³ + T*c2 + c3*epsilon/c5 + c6/c5 + c7 + c9

= T*c0*epsilon³ + T*c2 + (c3/c5)*epsilon + (c6/c5 + c7 + c9)

Has epsilon term but no epsilon³ (without T). Set c3=0:
= T*c0*epsilon³ + T*c2 + const

Missing epsilon³. Cannot match.

Hmm, but what if c4≠0? Then c3*epsilon/(c4*epsilon+c5) + c6/(c4*epsilon+c5) = (c3*epsilon+c6)/(c4*epsilon+c5). This is a rational function of epsilon. For GT we need a polynomial. This rational function would need to equal d*epsilon³ for some constant d, which is impossible for a ratio of degree-1 polynomials.

Candidate 18 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 19:
`c0*exp(c1*epsilon) + c2 + c3*epsilon^c4 + c5*epsilon + c6*log(c7*exp(T*c8 + c9*epsilon) + 1)`

The log term: if c8 and c9 are large positive, log(c7*exp(T*c8+c9*epsilon)+1) ≈ T*c8+c9*epsilon+log(c7). But this is an approximation, not exact. The "+1" inside the log prevents exact equivalence to a linear function.

Cannot match exactly.

Candidate 19 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 20:

= T*c1*epsilon³ + T*c0 + c5*epsilon³ + c3*epsilon + c4

GT = T*a*epsilon³ + T*b + d*epsilon³ + e

This has an extra c3*epsilon term. Set c3=0:
= T*c1*epsilon³ + T*c0 + c5*epsilon³ + c4 ✓

This matches! T*epsilon³ + T + epsilon³ + const.
